         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="sus2198-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/28b79c16-a920-4424-9a7b-03b0f9b2a61c/sus2198-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/28b79c16-a920-4424-9a7b-03b0f9b2a61c/sus2198-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/41038c60-5216-4771-a286-0dc9c1ef9721/sus2198-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/28b79c16-a920-4424-9a7b-03b0f9b2a61c/sus2198-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">FIGURE 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=sus2198-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsus2.198" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">(A) CV curves of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C in a scan rate range of 0.2–2.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. (B) Fitting lines of log <i>v</i> and log <i>i</i> at different redox peaks, (C) Separation of capacitive and diffusion contribution at 2.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. (D) Comparison of the capacitive contribution for four samples at different scan rates. (E) EIS spectra of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C at diverse cycles. (F) The working mechanism diagram of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C//NVP@C SIFCs device. (G) GCD profiles at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, (H) cycle stability at 1.0 and 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, (I) GCD profiles in a rate range of 0.2–5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and (J) rate performance of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C//NVP@C SIFCs device. CV, Cyclic voltammetry; EIS, electrochemical impedance spectroscopy; SIFC, sodium-ion full cell; GCD, galvanostatic charge/discharge.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Specifically, the <i>b</i> value, the fitted slope of the log(<i>i</i>) vs. log(<i>ν</i>) plot, holds significance since it stands for the rate-controlling factor of Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/de-insertion. Normally, the <i>b</i> value approaching 0.5 often indicates an ion diffusion-controlled process, whereas it that gets closer to 1.0 signifies a capacitive mechanism with a rapid reaction kinetic for Na<sup>+</sup>-storage. As for the calculated results for Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0005">5B</a>, the <i>b</i> values at three redox peaks, which fall between 0.5 and 1.0, illustrate two mechanisms work together to synergistically produce the exceptional electrochemical performance. For the purpose of being able to conduct a quantitative analysis of the contribution to the capacity at each course, the diffusion-controlled feature and the surface-capacitive reaction were achieved by establishing the current <i>i</i> at a stationary potential <i>V</i> as follows: <i>i</i> = <i>k</i><sub>1</sub> <i>v</i> + <i>k</i><sub>2</sub> <i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>.<span><sup><a href="#sus2198-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="sus2198-bib-0035_R_d83639732e1950" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J Mater Chem A">35</a>, <a href="#sus2198-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="sus2198-bib-0040_R_d83639732e1950" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Chem Eng J">40</a></sup></span> One could separate the capacitive process by computing the <i>k</i><sub>1</sub> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub> constants as the current percentage increases during the Na<sup>+</sup>-ion diffusion.<span><sup><a href="#sus2198-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="sus2198-bib-0039_R_d83639732e1962" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Small">39</a></sup></span> The surface-capacitive contributions of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C, Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS, Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4,</sub> and NiS are produced to be about 78.4%, 82.3%, 83.7%, and 84.1% at 0.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Subsequently, their capacitive contributions gradually develop up to 95.3%, 94.6%, 94.2%, and 92.1% as the scan rate increases to 2.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, and the typical voltage profiles for computed surface-capacitive current related to the tested current are also exhibited by the shaded area (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0005">5C</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12c,f,i</a>). Significantly, the capacitive contributions of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C are greater than those of other three electrodes at all scan rates (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0005">5D</a>). Undoubtedly, a greater proportion of the pseudocapacitive contribution may facilitate faster Na<sup>+</sup>-ion transmission and reaction dynamics, hence enhancing the rate capability of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C, which are advantageous due to the conductive outer-carbon skeleton and abundant heterogeneous interface. The evolution of reaction kinetics for the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C electrode under the cycling were estimated with the aid of the EIS spectra test, as depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0005">5E</a>. The initial wetting and activation of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C electrode is mostly responsible for the decline in <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> during the first 15 cycles.<span><sup><a href="#sus2198-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="sus2198-bib-0071_R_d83639732e2018" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Small">71</a></sup></span> But as the cycle goes on from 15th to 50th, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> steadily increases, attributable to the structural pulverization and the reduplicative manufacturing of the instability SEI layer.<span><sup><a href="#sus2198-bib-0072" class="bibLink tab-link" id="sus2198-bib-0072_R_d83639732e2024" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 72 - ACS Nano">72</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>Taking into account the impressive electrochemical capabilities in the half-cell, the usage possibilities of as-prepared Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C were assessed by fabricating sodium-ion full cells (SIFCs), which are packaged by using preactivated Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C electrode as the anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C (NVP@C) as the cathode to construct a Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C//NVP@C SIFCs. Concurrently, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0005">5F</a> manifests a diagrammatic representation of the working mechanism for Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C//NVP@C SIFCs during the charging–discharging processes. Meanwhile, the phase component and electrochemical capability of NVP@C are illustrated in Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> and S<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">16</a>. It is evident that NVP@C electrode achieves superior Na<sup>+</sup>-storage features involving attractive capacity and impressive cycle durability in a half cell system. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0005">5G</a>, the GCD profiles of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C//NVP@C SIFCs with a voltage range from 0.4 to 4.0&nbsp;V support the appealing capacities of about 641.4 and 627.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at the initial discharge and charge processes at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, affording an outstanding ICE of 97.8%, and then the coulombic efficiency increases rapidly to nearly 100% and stays there for the duration of the following cycles. Meanwhile, a pair of charge/discharge platforms, centered at around 3.5/3.1&nbsp;V, are what draw particular attention to the first GCD curves, which can be divided into two pairs (3.3/2.4 and 3.5/21.6&nbsp;V) beginning with the second cycle. Even after withstanding 60 consecutive loops (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0005">5H</a>), the SIFCs still provide the significant reversible capacity, with the values of approximately 407.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> and 315.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Notably, the successful usage of the charged coin-type SIFCs to illuminate commercial light-emitting diode (LED) lights screen displayed with the word “SIBs” (inset of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0005">5H</a>) is impressive and offers a great deal of potential for the practical application sustainability of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C for portable consumer electronics. The remarkable rate performance of SIFCs was also demonstrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0005">5I,J</a>, which yields reversible capacities of 624.8, 578.2, 503.6, 455.91, 386.0, and 305.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> for current rates of 0.2, 0.5, 1.0, 1.5, 3.0, and 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> in that sequence. Subsequently, the reversible capacity immediately changes to 532.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, once the rate resets to 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, producing a superior capacity retention of up to 85.2%. Generally, the different mass ratios between anode and cathode have an important influence on the electrochemical performance of full cells. Therefore, we adjusted the capacity ratio between the anode and cathode to explore the important influence on the electrochemical performance of full cells, the corresponding result is shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18a</a>. It is found that the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C//NVP@C SIFCs delivers the initial discharge and charge capacities of 533.9 and 529.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, when the ratio of anode to cathode is about 1:3. With the cycling progresses to the 60th cycle, the full cell obtains a reversible capacity of 386.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18b</a>). As the mass ratio between the anode and cathode increases to 1:5, the initial discharge and charge capacities of full cell are about 480.1 and 517.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18c</a>), subsequently, a reversible discharge capacity of 257. mAh g<sup>−1</sup> can be harvested after 60 cycles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18d</a>). These results are obviously smaller than that of the full cell with the ratio of anode to cathode electrode of 1:4, confirming that the optimal ratio between anode and cathode is about 1:4.</p>
         
         <p>In addition, we also integrated a commercial activated carbon (AC) cathode and preactivated Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C anode to create asymmetrical Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C//AC sodium ion hybrid capacitor (SIHCs) device that could further demonstrate the advantageous properties of heterostructure engineering in terms of electron and Na<sup>+</sup>-ion transport capability. Correspondingly, AC cathode, as illustrated in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, manifests remarkable electrochemical performance, featuring a good cyclic capability over 150 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. The SIHCs are capable of operating continuously at an operating voltage of 0.01–4.2&nbsp;V, and their CV profiles exist a slight deviation relative to the ideal rectangular shape (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19a</a>), which could be attributed to the various types of the charge storage mechanism between anode and cathode electrodes.<span><sup><a href="#sus2198-bib-0073" class="bibLink tab-link" id="sus2198-bib-0073_R_d83639732e2162" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 73 - Energy Environ Sci">73</a></sup></span> Meanwhile, more evidences from CV curves under various scan rates illustrate that the capacitive-controlled behavior drive the Na<sup>+</sup>-storage mechanism.<span><sup><a href="#sus2198-bib-0074" class="bibLink tab-link" id="sus2198-bib-0074_R_d83639732e2167" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 74 - Adv Sci">74</a></sup></span> Interestingly, even with a 60-fold increase in scan rate, the outlines of CV profiles essentially stay constant without encountering substantial distortion, proving the great rate capacity and superb reversibility. Similarly, the quasitriangular-shaped GCD curves at the current rate between 0.1 and 2.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> reflect a capacitive-dominated charge storage mechanism (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19b</a>). Additionally, the energy/power densities of SIHCs device are computed according to the GCD curves. Ragone plots of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C//AC SIHCs based on the total mass of both electrodes in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19c</a> illustrate that the SIHCs device features the superior gravimetric energy densities of 150.6/18.6&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at the gravimetric power densities of 210/3 150&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The evaluation of cycle durability is presented in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19d</a>. After 300 cycles, the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C//AC SIHCs device is able to keep 96.3% of its initial capacitance at a current rate of 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, as well as nearly 100% CE, proving its outstanding cycling stability and potential use in future practical applications.</p>
         
         <p>The main goal of the density functional theory (DFT) computation is to investigate the significance of constructing a strongly coupled heterointerface structure on superior electrochemical Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance. The correspondingly optimized Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS, Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and NiS structural configurations are potted in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>. According to the associated density of states (DOS) in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0006">6A–C</a>, one can see that all these models reveal outstanding metallicity characteristic with the electron states cross the Fermi level. Especially, the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS model presents the highest electron state at the Fermi level, thus signifying that the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS may possess a higher electronic conductivity in comparison to that of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> and NiS. The charge density difference of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a> reveals the intense charge transfer and exchange around the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS heterointerface, which can facilitate the adsorption and migration of Na<sup>+</sup>-ion. Additionally, the adsorbed Na<sup>+</sup> bonding features on Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS, Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and NiS configurations (denoted as Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS–Na, Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>–Na, and NiS–Na) are also uncovered through charge density difference analysis, as illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0006">6D</a>, which suggest the obvious charge transfer between Na atom and three models. The accumulation of electron surrounding the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS and the electron depletion of Na atom is visible. Meanwhile, a higher interaction occurs in the region between Na<sup>+</sup> and Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS compared to the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>–Na, and NiS–Na models, suggesting that Na<sup>+</sup> is more easily absorbed on the rich heterogeneous interface and synergistically promotes the Na<sup>+</sup>-storage performance. Bader charge analysis suggests that 0.823<i>e</i>, 0.819<i>e</i>, and 0.788<i>e</i> electrons are respectively transferred from Na atom to Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS, Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and NiS models. Obviously, the stronger charge transfer means a more significant Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption, which agrees well with some previous study.<span><sup><a href="#sus2198-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="sus2198-bib-0030_R_d83639732e2303" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Adv Funct Mater">30</a></sup></span> Moreover, the Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption binding energies (<i>E</i><sub>abs</sub>) and the corresponding absorption configurations are manifested in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#sus2198-fig-0006">6E</a>. The <i>E</i><sub>abs</sub> values are −1.89, −1.35, and −0.89&nbsp;eV for the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS, Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and NiS, respectively. Obviously, the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS shows the strongest Na<sup>+</sup>-ion adsorption among three structural models, which usually means its more favorable adsorption sites and better reaction kinetics. It is evident that all the computed results back up the experimental result that the formation of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS heterointerface can significantly enhance the electronic conductivity and Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption ability of TMCs, thereby endowing the superior electrochemical Na<sup>+</sup>-storage performance.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="sus2198-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/aa3ef518-2700-4bd9-8a4a-97e12f941b19/sus2198-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/aa3ef518-2700-4bd9-8a4a-97e12f941b19/sus2198-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0020e6b7-a42f-4174-a19d-3c4a661262e4/sus2198-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/aa3ef518-2700-4bd9-8a4a-97e12f941b19/sus2198-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">FIGURE 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=sus2198-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsus2.198" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">DOS of (A) Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS, (B) Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and (C) NiS models. (D) Charge density difference of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS, Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and NiS with one Na atom adsorption. The yellow and cyan regions denote the gain and loss of electrons, respectively. (E) Structural models of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS, Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and NiS with one Na adsorption and matched Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption energy. DOS, Density of states.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="sus2198-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="sus2198-sec-0030-title">3 CONCLUSIONS</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we developed an easy protocol for the design of a hierarchically hybrid material comprising hetero-Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS hollow nanosphere encapsulated within an ultrathin N-doped carbon matrix (Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C) through vulcanization, in situ dopamine polymerization, and carbonization using CoNi-glycerate as the template. The well-designed Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C architecture simultaneously integrates numerous merits including fast ion-diffusion and charge-transfer kinetics, superior electric conductivity, abundant Na<sup>+</sup>-transport channels, good structural stability, and adequate active reaction sites, thereby giving the constructed Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C-based batteries a significantly more desirable initial reversible capacity, rate capability, and cycling stability as comparison to other three reference samples. More specifically, the Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C electrode affords appealing discharge capacity reaching 310.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with an extremely small capacity fading of only 0.05% each cycle even after 2 400 cycles. Ex situ XRD together with ex situ XPS and TEM characterizations verified the insertion–conversion mechanism and strong reversibility of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C. Additionally, the SIFC and hybrid capacitor combined with an NVP@C or AC cathode and Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C anode exhibits good electrochemical characteristics, such as exceptional rate capability, impressive cycle stability, and specific capacity, showcasing the outstanding feasibility for practical use. According to the DFT calculation, the favorable electrochemical features of Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>/NiS@N-C were associated with its high conductivity and excellent Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption ability upon cycling process. This study not only offers a unique viewpoint on the usage of heterogeneous metal sulfides in high-efficiency Na<sup>+</sup>-storage fields, but also overcomes the structural instability and slow reaction kinetics that frequently exists in SIBs systems.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
